## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch-reactor ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ordinary differential equation for concentration A versus time t, which is the standard modeling form for chemical kinetics in a batch or well-mixed reactor. Typical relationships are mass-action rate laws (functions of A) possibly with explicit time dependence (non-autonomous kinetics due to changing conditions like temperature, light, or catalyst activity).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or saturated catalyst where rate is independent of A)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decomposition; dilute-limit mass action)
- Source + first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (continuous formation with linear consumption; relaxation to steady state)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or dimerization in a single-species model)
- General power-law (n-th order) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical kinetics; non-integer orders common in complex mechanisms)
- Fractional-order (diffusion/transport-limited) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**0.5 (effective rate under diffusion control or fractal-like kinetics)
- Reversible first-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * (c2 - A) (A ⇌ B with B approximated by c2 - A in a closed system)
- Autocatalytic / Prout–Tompkins-type: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating reaction with depletion/finite capacity)
- Autoinhibition / competing growth and depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (net production at low A and inhibition/consumption at high A)
- Substrate inhibition (Haldane-like single-variable form): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (rate increases then decreases at high A due to inhibitory complexation)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate accelerates/decelerates with time due to temperature ramp or catalyst activation/deactivation)
- Periodically forced kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (photochemistry or oscillatory external forcing of the rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), the system is autonomous; trajectories are time-shift invariant and kinetics are governed by A alone.
- A strictly negative term proportional to A (e.g., -c*A) indicates exponential decay with constant half-life; proportional to A**2 indicates decay rate accelerates with concentration.
- Presence of a constant source term (+c0) implies a nonzero steady state where production balances consumption (often A* = c0/c1 in linear loss models).
- Terms like A*(c1 - A) suggest self-acceleration at low A but depletion/finite-capacity limitation at high A, typical of autocatalysis or limited reactant availability.
- A denominator with 1 + c*A + c*A**2 indicates saturation and/or inhibition mechanisms (complex formation, crowding, catalyst saturation) producing non-monotone rate vs A.
- Explicit exp(c*t) multiplying A indicates a time-evolving rate constant (e.g., heating/cooling program, catalyst aging/activation) rather than intrinsic concentration dependence.
- Sin(c*t) modulation points to periodic external forcing (light/dark cycles, feed pulsing) and can create apparent oscillations in A even with simple underlying kinetics.
- Non-integer powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) often signal effective kinetics controlled by transport, heterogeneous surfaces, or aggregated multi-step mechanisms rather than elementary mass action.
